TOOLKIT & METHODOLOGY\n\n## 3.1 TOOL SELECTION PRINCIPLES\n\n- IMAGE TOOL PRIORITY:\n  * For any request involving image creation, modification, style change, or visual design, ALWAYS prefer the Image Tool.\n  * Do NOT describe images purely in text when an image output is expected.\n  * If an image result is required, the Image Tool is mandatory.\n\n- CLI TOOLS PREFERENCE:\n  * Always prefer CLI tools over Python scripts when possible\n  * CLI tools are generally faster and more efficient for:\n    1. Synchronous Commands (blocking):\n      * You can omit `blocking`, as it defaults to true\n      * Use for quick operations that complete within 60 seconds\n      * Commands run directly and wait for completion\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="default" blocking="true">\n        ls -l\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n        (or simply omit the blocking parameter as it defaults to true)\n      * IMPORTANT: Do not use for long-running operations as they will timeout after 60 seconds\n\n  2. Asynchronous Commands (non-blocking):\n      * Use `blocking="false"` for any command that might take longer than 60 seconds or for starting background services\n      * Commands run in background and return immediately\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="dev" blocking="false">\n        npm run dev\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n      * Common use cases:\n        - Development servers (Next.js, React, etc.)\n        - Build processes\n        - Long-running data processing\n        - Background services\n\n- Session Management:\n  * Each command must specify a session_name\n  * Use consistent session names for related commands\n  * Different sessions are isolated from each other\n  * Example: Use "build" session for build commands, "dev" for development servers\n  * Sessions maintain state between commands\n\n- Command Execution Guidelines:\n  * For commands that might take longer than 60 seconds, ALWAYS use run_async="true"\n  * Do not rely on increasing timeout for long-running commands\n  * Use proper session names for organization\n  * Chain commands with && for sequential execution\n  * Use | for piping output between commands\n  * Redirect output to files for long-running processes\n\n- Avoid commands requiring confirmation; actively use -y or -f flags for automatic confirmation\n- Avoid commands with excessive output; save to files when necessary\n- Chain multiple commands with operators to minimize interruptions and improve efficiency:\n  1. Use && for sequential execution: `command1 && command2 && command3`\n  2. Use || for fallback execution: `command1 || command2`\n  3. Use ; for unconditional execution: `command1; command2`\n  4. Use | for piping output: `command1 | command2`\n  5. Use > and >> for output redirection: `command > file` or `command >> file`\n- Use pipe operator to pass command outputs, simplifying operations\n- Use non-interactive `bc` for simple calculations, Python for complex math; never calculate mentally\n- Use `uptime` command when users explicitly request sandbox status check or wake-up\n\n## 3.3 CODE DEVELOPMENT PRACTICES\n- CODING:\n  * Must save code to files before execution; direct code input to interpreter commands is forbidden\n  * Write Python code for complex mathematical calculations and analysis\n  * Use search tools to find solutions when encountering unfamiliar problems\n  * For index.html, use deployment tools directly, or package everything into a zip file and provide it as a message attachment\n  * When creating web interfaces, always create CSS files first before HTML to ensure proper styling and design consistency\n  * For images, use real image URLs from sources like unsplash.com, pexels.com, pixabay.com, giphy.com, or wikimedia.org instead of creating placeholder images; use placeholder.com only as a last resort\n\n- WEBSITE DEPLOYMENT:\n  * Only use the \'deploy\' tool when users explicitly request permanent deployment to a production environment\n  * The deploy tool publishes static HTML+CSS+JS sites to a public URL using S3 web Pages\n  * If the same name is used for deployment, it will redeploy to the same project as before\n  * For temporary or development purposes, serve files locally instead of using the deployment tool\n  * When editing HTML files, always share the preview URL provided by the automatically running HTTP server with the user\n  * The preview URL is automatically generated and available in the tool results when creating or editing HTML files\n  * When deploying, ensure all assets (images, scripts, stylesheets) use relative paths to work correctly\n\n- PYTHON EXECUTION: Create reusable modules with proper error handling and logging. Use for precise text matching\n  2. Combine with CLI tools for powerful searches\n  3. Save complex patterns to files for reuse\n  4. Test patterns with small samples first\n  5. Use extended regex (-E) for complex patterns\n- Data Processing Workflow:\n  1. Use grep to locate relevant files\n  2. Use head/tail to preview content\n  3. Use awk for data extraction\n  4. WORKFLOW MANAGEMENT\n\n## 5.1 AUTONOMOUS WORKFLOW SYSTEM\nYou operate through a self-maintained todo.md file that serves as your central source of truth and execution roadmap:\n\n1. Upon receiving a task, immediately create a lean, focused todo.md with essential sections covering the task lifecycle\n2. Each section contains specific, actionable subtasks based on complexity - use only as many as needed, no more\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Adapt the plan as needed while maintaining its integrity as your execution compass\n\n## 5.2 TODO.MD FILE STRUCTURE AND USAGE\nThe todo.md file is your primary working document and action plan:\n\n1. Contains the complete list of tasks you MUST complete to fulfill the user\'s request\n2. Format with clear sections, each containing specific tasks marked with [ ] (incomplete) or [x] (complete)\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Before every action, consult your todo.md to determine which task to tackle next\n6. The todo.md serves as your instruction set - if a task is in todo.md, you are responsible for completing it\n7. Update the todo.md as you make progress, adding new tasks as needed and marking completed ones\n8. Never delete tasks from todo.md - instead mark them complete with [x] to maintain a record of your work\n9. Once ALL tasks in todo.md are marked complete [x], you MUST call either the \'complete\' state or \'ask\' tool to signal task completion\n10. SCOPE CONSTRAINT: Focus on completing existing tasks before adding new ones; avoid continuously expanding scope\n11. CAPABILITY AWARENESS: Only add tasks that are achievable with your available tools and capabilities\n12. FINALITY: After marking a section complete, do not reopen it or add new tasks unless explicitly directed by the user\n13. STOPPING CONDITION: If you\'ve made 3 consecutive updates to todo.md without completing any tasks, reassess your approach and either simplify your plan or **use the \'ask\' tool to seek user guidance.**\n14. COMPLETION VERIFICATION: Only mark a task as [x] complete when you have concrete evidence of completion\n15. SIMPLICITY: Keep your todo.md lean and direct with clear actions, avoiding unnecessary verbosity or granularity\n\n## 5.3 EXECUTION PHILOSOPHY\nYour approach is deliberately methodical and persistent:\n\n1. Operate in a continuous loop until explicitly stopped\n2. Execute one step at a time, following a consistent loop: evaluate state → select tool → execute → provide narrative update → track progress\n3. Every action is guided by your todo.md, consulting it before selecting any tool\n4. Thoroughly verify each completed step before moving forward\n5. **Provide Markdown-formatted narrative updates directly in your responses** to keep the user informed of your progress, explain your thinking, and clarify the next steps. Use headers, brief descriptions, and context to make your process transparent.\n6. CRITICALLY IMPORTANT: Continue running in a loop until either:\n  - Using the **\'ask\' tool (THE ONLY TOOL THE USER CAN RESPOND TO)** to wait for essential user input (this pauses the loop)\n  - Using the \'complete\' tool when ALL tasks are finished\n7. For casual conversation:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** to properly end the conversation and wait for user input (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n8. For tasks:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** when you need essential user input to proceed (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n  - Provide **narrative updates** frequently in your responses to keep the user informed without requiring their input\n  - Use \'complete\' only when ALL tasks are finished\n9. MANDATORY COMPLETION:\n  - IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after ALL tasks in todo.md are marked [x]\n  - NO additional commands or verifications after all tasks are complete\n  - NO further exploration or information gathering after completion\n  - NO redundant checks or validations after completion\n  - FAILURE to use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after task completion is a critical error\n\n## 5.4 TASK MANAGEMENT CYCLE\n1. STATE EVALUATION: Examine Todo.md for priorities, analyze recent Tool Results for environment understanding, and review past actions for context\n2. TOOL SELECTION: Choose exactly one tool that advances the current todo item\n3. EXECUTION: Wait for tool execution and observe results\n4. **NARRATIVE UPDATE:** Provide a **Markdown-formatted** narrative update directly in your response before the next tool call. Include explanations of what you\'ve done, what you\'re about to do, and why. Use headers, brief paragraphs, and formatting to enhance readability.\n5. PROGRESS TRACKING: Update todo.md with completed items and new tasks\n6. METHODICAL ITERATION: Repeat until section completion\n7. SECTION TRANSITION: Document completion and move to next section\n8. COMPLETION: IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' when ALL tasks are finished\n\n# 6. CONTENT CREATION\n\n## 6.1 WRITING GUIDELINES\n- Write content in continuous paragraphs using varied sentence lengths for engaging prose; avoid list formatting\n- Use prose and paragraphs by default; provide detailed content with proper citations\n- Strictly follow requirements in writing rules, and avoid using list formats in any files except todo.md\n\n## 6.2 DESIGN GUIDELINES\n- For any design-related task, first create the design in HTML+CSS to ensure maximum flexibility\n- Designs should be created with print-friendliness in mind - use appropriate margins, page breaks, and printable color schemes\n- After creating designs in HTML+CSS, convert directly to PDF as the final output format\n- When designing multi-page documents, ensure consistent styling and proper page numbering\n- Test print-readiness by confirming designs display correctly in print preview mode\n- For complex designs, test different media queries including print media type\n- Package all design assets (HTML, CSS, images, and PDF output) together when delivering final results\n- Ensure all fonts are properly embedded or use web-safe fonts to maintain design integrity in the PDF output\n- Set appropriate page sizes (A4, Letter, etc.) in the CSS using @page rules for consistent PDF rendering\n\n## Image Guidelines\n- ALWAYS use the Image Tool for image generation or image editing tasks\n- Write a single self-contained image prompt before calling the Image Tool\n- Clearly describe the main subject and overall composition\n- Explicitly specify the intended visual style and aesthetic\n- Provide exact text content if text is required; otherwise state “no text”\n- For image editing, clearly state what changes and what must remain unchanged\n- Request the image first if an edit is requested without a provided image\n- Ask clarification questions only when essential information is missing\n\n# 7. COMMUNICATION & USER INTERACTION\n\n## 7.1 CONVERSATIONAL INTERACTIONS\nFor casual conversation and social interactions:\n  - ALWAYS use **\'ask\'** tool to end the conversation and wait for user input (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n  - NEVER use \'complete\' for casual conversation\n  - Keep responses friendly and natural\n  - Adapt to user\'s communication style\n  - Ask follow-up questions when appropriate (**using \'ask\'**)\n  - Show interest in user\'s responses\n\n## 7.2 COMMUNICATION PROTOCOLS\n- **Core Principle: Communicate proactively, directly, and descriptively throughout your responses.**\n\n- **Narrative-Style Communication:**\n  * Integrate descriptive Markdown-formatted text directly in your responses before, between, and after tool calls\n  * Use a conversational yet efficient tone that conveys what you\'re doing and why\n  * Structure your communication with Markdown headers, brief paragraphs, and formatting for enhanced readability\n  * Balance detail with conciseness - be informative without being verbose\n\n- **Communication Structure:**\n  * Begin tasks with a brief overview of your plan\n  * Provide context headers like `## Planning`, `### Researching`, `## Creating File`, etc.\n  * Before each tool call, explain what you\'re about to do and why\n  * After significant results, summarize what you learned or accomplished\n  * Use transitions between major steps or sections\n  * Maintain a clear narrative flow that makes your process transparent to the user\n\n- **Message Types & Usage:**\n  * **Direct Narrative:** Embed clear, descriptive text directly in your responses explaining your actions, reasoning, and observations\n  * **\'ask\' (USER CAN RESPOND):** Use ONLY for essential needs requiring user input (clarification, confirmation, options, missing info, validation). This blocks execution until user responds.\n  * Minimize blocking operations (\'ask\'); maximize narrative descriptions in your regular responses.\n- **Deliverables:**\n  * Attach all relevant files with the **\'ask\'** tool when asking a question related to them, or when delivering final results before completion.\n  * Always include representable files as attachments when using \'ask\' - this includes HTML files, presentations, writeups, visualizations, reports, and any other viewable content.\n  * For any created files that can be viewed or presented (such as index.html, slides, documents, charts, etc.), always attach them to the \'ask\' tool to ensure the user can immediately see the results.\n  * Share results and deliverables before entering complete state (use \'ask\' with attachments as appropriate).\n  * Ensure users have access to all necessary resources.\n\n- Communication Tools Summary:\n  * **\'ask\':** Essential questions/clarifications. BLOCKS execution. **USER CAN RESPOND.**\n  * **text via markdown format:** Frequent UI/progress updates. NON-BLOCKING. **USER CANNOT RESPOND.**\n  * Include the \'attachments\' parameter with file paths or URLs when sharing resources (works with both \'ask\').\n  * **\'complete\':** Only when ALL tasks are finished and verified. Terminates execution.\n\n- Tool Results: Carefully analyze all tool execution results to inform your next actions. **Use regular text in markdown format to communicate significant results or progress.**\n\n## 7.3 ATTACHMENT PROTOCOL\n- **CRITICAL: ALL VISUALIZATIONS MUST BE ATTACHED:**\n  * When using the \'ask\' or \'complete\' tool, ALWAYS attach ALL visualizations, markdown files, charts, graphs, reports, and any viewable content created.\n  * This includes but is not limited to: HTML files, PDF documents, markdown files, images, data visualizations, presentations, reports, dashboards, UI mockups and externally accessible results.\n  * NEVER mention a visualization or viewable content without attaching it\n  * If you\'ve created multiple visualizations, attach ALL of them\n  * Always make visualizations available to the user BEFORE marking tasks as complete\n  * For web applications or interactive content, always attach the main HTML file\n  * When creating data analysis results, charts must be attached, not just described\n  * Remember: If the user should SEE it, you must ATTACH it with the \'ask\' tool\n  * Verify that ALL visual outputs have been attached before proceeding\n\n- **Attachment Checklist:**\n  * Data visualizations (charts, graphs, plots)\n  * Web interfaces (HTML/CSS/JS files)\n  * Reports and documents (PDF, HTML)\n  * Presentation materials\n  * Images and diagrams\n  * Interactive dashboards\n  * Analysis results with visual components\n  * UI designs and mockups\n  * Any file intended for user viewing or interaction\n\n\n# 8. "malware_family": "Sunburst",\n  "confidence": "high",\n  "first_seen": "2020-12-01T00:00:00Z",\n  "last_seen": "2026-01-15T00:00:00Z",\n  "description": "Command and control server",\n  "source": "V-Sentinel Research",\n  "references": [\n    "https://attack.mitre.org/groups/G0016/",\n    "https://www.fireeye.com/blog.html"\n  ],\n  "tags": ["c2", "apt", "espionage"],\n  "attribution_confidence": "high"\n}\n```\n\n### IOC Type Guidelines\n\n#### IP Addresses\n- Must be valid IPv4 or IPv6 addresses\n- Exclude reserved/private ranges (RFC 1918)\n- Provide confidence level (low, medium, high)\n- Include port information if applicable\n\n#### Domain Names\n- Must be fully qualified domain names (FQDNs)\n- Exclude wildcards unless specifically targeting subdomains\n- Include WHOIS registration dates\n- Provide DNS resolution history\n\n#### File Hashes\n- Must include at least SHA256\n- Include MD5 and SHA1 if available\n- Provide file size and type\n- Include compilation timestamps if available\n\n#### URLs\n- Must include full protocol (http/https)\n- Sanitize sensitive parameters\n- Include URL path patterns\n- Provide HTTP method if relevant\n\n### IOC Submission Checklist\n\n- [ ] IOC format is valid JSON\n- [ ] All required fields are present\n- [ ] Confidence level is specified\n- [ ] Attribution information is included\n- [ ] Source references are provided\n- [ ] First and last seen dates are accurate\n- [ ] IOC is validated using `scripts/validate_iocs.py`\n- [ ] No duplicate entries exist\n- [ ] No false positives identified\n\n### Example Submission\n\n```json\n{\n  "id": "ioc-001",\n  "type": "domain",\n  "value": "malicious-c2[.]example[.]com",\n  "threat_actor": "Lazarus Group",\n  "campaign": "Operation AppleJeus",\n  "malware_family": "AppleJeus",\n  "confidence": "high",\n  "first_seen": "2024-06-15T00:00:00Z",\n  "last_seen": "2026-01-10T00:00:00Z",\n  "description": "Command and control domain used in financial theft campaigns targeting cryptocurrency exchanges",\n  "source": "V-Sentinel Research",\n  "references": [\n    "https://attack.mitre.org/groups/G0032/",\n    "https://www.kaspersky.com/resource-center/threats/applejeus"\n  ],\n  "tags": ["c2", "financial", "cryptocurrency", "lazarus"],\n  "attribution_confidence": "high"\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 📜 Adding Detection Rules\n\n### YARA Rules\n\n```yara\nrule Emotet_Dropper {\n    meta:\n        description = "Detects Emotet dropper payload"\n        threat_actor = "TA542"\n        malware_family = "Emotet"\n        confidence = "high"\n        date = "2026-01-15"\n        reference = "https://attack.mitre.org/groups/G0095/"\n    \n    strings:\n        $s1 = { 4D 5A 90 00 }  // MZ header\n        $s2 = "powershell.exe" nocase\n        $s3 = "Invoke-Expression" nocase\n        $s4 = "https://api[.]ipify[.]org" ascii wide\n    \n    condition:\n        uint16(0) == 0x5A4D and\n        all of ($s*)\n}\n```\n\n### Snort/Suricata Rules\n\n```snort\nalert tcp $EXTERNAL_NET any -> $HOME_NET 445 (msg:"ET TROJAN Emotet C2 Traffic"; flow:established,to_server; content:"|50 4F 53 54 20|"; depth:4; content:"User-Agent:"; content:"Microsoft-CryptoAPI"; distance:0; reference:url,attack.mitre.org/groups/G0095/; sid:2026001; rev:1;)\n```\n\n### Sigma Rules\n\n```yaml\ntitle: Potential Emotet Macro Execution\nid: 1a0e5b1c-2d3e-4f5a-9b8c-7d6e5f4a3b2c\ndescription: Detects potential Emotet macro execution in Office documents\nstatus: stable\nauthor: V-Sentinel Research\ndate: 2026/01/15\nreferences:\n    - https://attack.mitre.org/groups/G0095/\ntags:\n    - attack.initial_access\n    - attack.t1566.001\nlogsource:\n    product: windows\n    service: security\ndetection:\n    selection:\n        EventID: 4688\n        NewProcessName|endswith:\n            - \'\\winword.exe\'\n            - \'\\excel.exe\'\n            - \'\\powerpnt.exe\'\n        CommandLine|contains:\n            - \'powershell.exe\'\n            - \'cmd.exe /c\'\n    condition: selection\nfalsepositives:\n    - Legitimate macro usage\nlevel: high\n```\n\n### Rule Submission Checklist\n\n- [ ] Rule syntax is valid\n- [ ] Metadata is complete (description, author, date, references)\n- [ ] MITRE ATT&CK techniques are mapped\n- [ ] False positive rate is documented\n- [ ] Rule has been tested against known samples\n- [ ] Performance impact is assessed\n- [ ] Rule follows naming conventions\n- [ ] Documentation includes usage examples\n\n---\n\n## 🧪 Testing and Validation\n\n### Running Validation\n\n```bash\n# Validate all IOCs\npython scripts/validate_iocs.py --path iocs/\n\n# Validate specific category\npython scripts/validate_iocs.py --path iocs/apt/\n\n# Generate detailed report\npython scripts/validate_iocs.py --path iocs/ --report validation_report.txt\n\n# Test rule syntax\npython scripts/test_rules.py --path rules/yara/\n\n# Run integration tests\npytest tests/\n```\n\n### Automated CI/CD\n\nAll contributions are automatically validated through CI/CD:\n- JSON schema validation\n- IOC format checking\n- Rule syntax validation\n- Duplicate detection\n- False positive scanning\n\n---\n\n## 📊 Attribution Guidelines\n\n### Confidence Levels\n\n- **High**: Multiple independent sources, technical evidence, official attribution\n- **Medium**: Technical evidence with some attribution uncertainty\n- **Low**: Single source, circumstantial evidence, industry consensus\n\n### Attribution Standards\n\n1. **Technical Evidence**: Code similarities, infrastructure overlap, TTPs\n2. **Victimology**: Target geography, industry sector, timing\n3. **Operational Security**: Language, time zones, tool preferences\n4. **Intelligence Sources**: Private threat feeds, government advisories, industry reports\n\n### When NOT to Attribute\n\n- Single-source attribution without corroboration\n- Speculative connections without technical evidence\n- Politically motivated attributions\n- Commercially motivated claims\n\n---\n\n## 🚨 False Positive Management\n\n### Reducing False Positives\n\n1. **Specificity**: Use highly specific patterns\n2. **Context**: Include contextual information\n3. **Testing**: Test against legitimate traffic\n4. **Documentation**: Document known FPs\n5. **Tuning**: Provide tuning parameters\n\n### Reporting False Positives\n\nIf you encounter false positives:\n\n```bash\n# Report via GitHub Issue\ngh issue create --title "False Positive: [IOC/RULE ID]" \\\n  --body "Description of false positive scenario"\n```\n\nInclude:\n- IOC or rule ID\n- False positive scenario\n- Legitimate context\n- Suggested improvements\n\n---\n\n## 📝 Documentation Standards\n\n### Threat Analysis Reports\n\n```markdown\n# Threat Analysis: [Campaign Name]\n\n## Executive Summary\nBrief overview of the threat actor, objectives, and impact.\n\n## Technical Analysis\n### Infrastructure\n- IPs, domains, certificates\n- Hosting providers\n- Network topology\n\n### Malware Analysis\n- Family description\n- Capabilities\n- Persistence mechanisms\n\n### Tactics, Techniques, and Procedures\n- MITRE ATT&CK mapping\n- Kill chain analysis\n- Timeline of activity\n\n## Attribution\n- Evidence supporting attribution\n- Confidence level\n- References\n\n## IOCs\nList of related indicators\n\n## Detection\nRecommended detection rules and hunting queries\n```\n\n---\n\n## 🔄 Pull Request Process\n\n### Before Submitting\n\n1. **Validate**: Run `scripts/validate_iocs.py`\n2. **Test**: Run `pytest tests/`\n3. **Format**: Ensure consistent formatting\n4. **Document**: Update relevant documentation\n5. **Commit**: Use clear commit messages\n\n### Commit Message Format\n\n```\n[TYPE]: Brief description\n\nDetailed explanation of changes:\n- What was changed\n- Why it was changed\n- How it was tested\n\nRelated issues: #123\n```\n\nTypes: `feat`, `fix`, `docs`, `test`, `chore`\n\n### Submitting PR\n\n```bash\n# Push your branch\ngit push origin feature/your-contribution\n\n# Create pull request\ngh pr create --title "Add IOCs for [Threat Actor]" \\\n  --body "Description of changes"\n```\n\n### PR Review Process\n\n1. Automated checks must pass\n2. Manual review by security researchers\n3. Attribution verification\n4. False positive assessment\n5. Documentation review\n6. Approval and merge\n\n---\n\n## 🎖️ Recognition\n\nContributors are recognized in:\n- README.md contributor list\n- CHANGELOG.md with attribution\n- GitHub contributors graph\n- Annual security research report\n\n---\n\n## 📞 Contact\n\n- **Contributions**: security-research@vantis.ai\n- **Questions**: Use GitHub Issues\n- **Security Issues**: security@vantis.ai\n\n---\n\n## 📜 Code of Conduct\n\n- Be respectful and constructive\n- Provide evidence for claims\n- Acknowledge limitations\n- Collaborate openly\n- Follow responsible disclosure\n\nThank you for contributing to V-Sentinel IOCs! 🙏\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

file_path="V-Sentinel-IOCs/scripts/format_converter.py">\n#!/usr/bin/env python3\n"""\nV-Sentinel IOC Format Converter\nConverts IOCs between JSON, CSV, STIX, and OpenIOC formats\n"""\n\nimport json\nimport csv\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport argparse\nfrom datetime import datetime\nfrom typing import Dict, List, Any, Optional\nimport uuid\n\n\nclass IOCFormatConverter:\n    """Converts IOCs between different formats"""\n    \n    def __init__(self):\n        self.converted_count = 0\n        self.failed_count = 0\n    \n    def load_iocs(self, input_file: str) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:\n        """Load IOCs from JSON file"""\n        if not os.path.exists(input_file):\n            raise FileNotFoundError(f"Input file not found: {input_file}")\n        \n        with open(input_file, \'r\') as f:\n            data = json.load(f)\n        \n        # Handle different JSON structures\n        if isinstance(data, dict):\n            if "indicators" in data:\n                return data["indicators"]\n            elif "type" in data and "value" in data:\n                return [data]\n            else:\n                raise ValueError("Invalid IOC structure")\n        elif isinstance(data, list):\n            return data\n        else:\n            raise ValueError("Invalid data type")\n    \n    def convert_to_csv(self, iocs: List[Dict[str, Any]], output_file: str) -> bool:\n        """Convert IOCs to CSV format"""\n        try:\n            # Define CSV fields\n            fieldnames = [\n                "id", "type", "value", "confidence", "threat_actor",\n                "campaign", "malware_family", "first_seen", "last_seen",\n                "description", "tags"\n            ]\n            \n            with open(output_file, \'w\', newline=\'\', in iocs:\n                    # Flatten tags array\n                    if "tags" in ioc and isinstance(ioc["tags"], list):\n                        ioc["tags"] = ", ".join(ioc["tags"])\n                    \n                    writer.writerow(ioc)\n                    self.converted_count += 1\n            \n            return True\n        except Exception as e:\n            print(f"Error converting to CSV: {e}", file=sys.stderr)\n            self.failed_count += 1\n            return False\n    \n    def convert_to_stix(self, iocs: List[Dict[str, Any]], output_file: str) -> bool:\n        """Convert IOCs to STIX 2.1 format"""\n        try:\n            stix_bundle = {\n                "type": "bundle",\n                "id": f"bundle--{str(uuid.uuid4())}",\n                "spec_version": "2.1",\n                "objects": []\n            }\n            \n            # Create identity object for V-Sentinel\n            identity = {\n                "type": "identity",\n                "id": "identity--v-sentinel-research",\n                "name": "V-Sentinel Security Research",\n                "identity_class": "organization"\n            }\n            stix_bundle["objects"].append(identity)\n            \n            # Create indicator objects for each IOC\n            for ioc in iocs:\n                indicator = {\n                    "type": "indicator",\n                    "id": f"indicator--{str(uuid.uuid4())}",\n                    "created": datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S.%fZ"),\n                    "modified": datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S.%fZ"),\n                    "name": ioc.get("description", ioc["value"]),\n                    "description": ioc.get("description", ""),\n                    "indicator_types": ["malicious-activity"],\n                    "pattern": self._create_stix_pattern(ioc),\n                    "valid_from": ioc.get("first_seen", datetime.now().isoformat() + "Z"),\n                    "created_by_ref": "identity--v-sentinel-research"\n                }\n                \n                # Add confidence level\n                if "confidence" in ioc:\n                    confidence_map = {"low": 15, "medium": 50, "high": 85}\n                    indicator["confidence"] = confidence_map.get(ioc["confidence"], 50)\n                \n                # Add labels/tags\n                if "tags" in ioc:\n                    indicator["labels"] = ioc["tags"]\n                \n                # Add threat actor reference\n                if "threat_actor" in ioc:\n                    threat_actor_id = f"intrusion-set--{ioc[\'threat_actor\'].lower().replace(\' \', \'-\')}"\n                    indicator["pattern"] = indicator["pattern"].replace("threat_actor", threat_actor_id)\n                \n                stix_bundle["objects"].append(indicator)\n                self.converted_count += 1\n            \n            with open(output_file, \'w\') as f:\n                json.dump(stix_bundle, f, indent=2)\n            \n            return True\n        except Exception as e:\n            print(f"Error converting to STIX: {e}", file=sys.stderr)\n            self.failed_count += 1\n            return False\n    \n    def convert_to_openioc(self, iocs: List[Dict[str, Any]], output_file: str) -> bool:\n        """Convert IOCs to OpenIOC XML format"""\n        try:\n            xml_lines = []\n            xml_lines.append(\'<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>\')\n            xml_lines.append(\'<OpenIOC xmlns="http://schemas.mandiant.com/2010/ioc" xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" xmlns:ioc="http://schemas.mandiant.com/2010/ioc" xsi:schemaLocation="http://schemas.mandiant.com/2010/ioc ioc.xsd">\')\n            xml_lines.append(\'  <definition>\')\n            xml_lines.append(f\'    <short_description>Generated by V-Sentinel IOC Converter</short_description>\')\n            xml_lines.append(f\'    <description>Converted {len(iocs)} indicators</description>\')\n            xml_lines.append(f\'    <authored_by>V-Sentinel Security Research</authored_by>\')\n            xml_lines.append(f\'    <authored_date>{datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S")}</authored_date>\')\n            xml_lines.append(\'    <links/>\')\n            \n            for ioc in iocs:\n                xml_lines.append(\'    <Indicator id="{}" operator="OR">\'.format(ioc.get("id", str(uuid.uuid4()))))\n                xml_lines.append(\'      <Context document="{}" search="{}" type="{}">\'.format(\n                    ioc.get("threat_actor", "ThreatActor"),\n                    ioc.get("description", ioc["value"]),\n                    ioc["type"]\n                ))\n                xml_lines.append(\'        <ContentItem type="{}">\'.format(ioc["type"]))\n                \n                if ioc["type"] == "ip":\n                    xml_lines.append(\'          <Address condition="is">{}</Address>\'.format(ioc["value"]))\n                elif ioc["type"] == "domain":\n                    xml_lines.append(\'          <DomainItem condition="is">{}</DomainItem>\'.format(ioc["value"]))\n                elif ioc["type"] == "url":\n                    xml_lines.append(\'          <Url condition="is">{}</Url>\'.format(ioc["value"]))\n                elif ioc["type"] == "hash":\n                    xml_lines.append(\'          <Hash condition="is" type="{}">{}</Hash>\'.format(\n                        ioc.get("hash_type", "SHA-256"), ioc["value"]\n                    ))\n                elif ioc["type"] == "email":\n                    xml_lines.append(\'          <EmailItem condition="is">{}</EmailItem>\'.format(ioc["value"]))\n                \n                xml_lines.append(\'        </ContentItem>\')\n                xml_lines.append(\'      </Context>\')\n                xml_lines.append(\'    </Indicator>\')\n                self.converted_count += 1\n            \n            xml_lines.append(\'  </definition>\')\n            xml_lines.append(\'</OpenIOC>\')\n            \n            with open(output_file, \'w\') as f:\n                f.write(\'\\n\'.join(xml_lines))\n            \n            return True\n        except Exception as e:\n            print(f"Error converting to OpenIOC: {e}", file=sys.stderr)\n            self.failed_count += 1\n            return False\n    \n    def convert_to_json(self, iocs: List[Dict[str, Any]], output_file: str, pretty: bool = True) -> bool:\n        """Convert IOCs to formatted JSON"""\n        try:\n            with open(output_file, \'w\') as f:\n                if pretty:\n                    json.dump(iocs, f, indent=2)\n                else:\n                    json.dump(iocs, f)\n            self.converted_count += len(iocs)\n            return True\n        except Exception as e:\n            print(f"Error converting to JSON: {e}", file=sys.stderr)\n            self.failed_count += 1\n            return False\n    \n    def _create_stix_pattern(self, ioc: Dict[str, Any]) -> str:\n        """Create STIX pattern from IOC"""\n        ioc_type = ioc["type"]\n        value = ioc["value"]\n        \n        pattern_map = {\n            "ip": f"[ipv4-addr:value = \'{value}\']",\n            "domain": f"[domain-name:value = \'{value}\']",\n            "url": f"[url:value = \'{value}\']",\n            "hash": f"[file:hashes.\'{ioc.get(\\"hash_type\\", \\"SHA-256\\")}\' = \'{value}\']",\n            "email": f"[email-addr:value = \'{value}\']"\n        }\n        \n        return pattern_map.get(ioc_type, f"[{ioc_type}:value = \'{value}\']")\n    \n    def convert(self, input_file: str, output_file: str, target_format: str) -> bool:\n        """Main conversion method"""\n        try:\n            # Load IOCs\n            iocs = self.load_iocs(input_file)\n            print(f"Loaded {len(iocs)} IOCs from {input_file}")\n            \n            # Convert based on target format\n            if target_format == "csv":\n                success = self.convert_to_csv(iocs, output_file)\n            elif target_format == "stix":\n                success = self.convert_to_stix(iocs, output_file)\n            elif target_format == "openioc":\n                success = self.convert_to_openioc(iocs, output_file)\n            elif target_format == "json":\n                success = self.convert_to_json(iocs, output_file)\n            else:\n                raise ValueError(f"Unsupported format: {target_format}")\n            \n            if success:\n                print(f"✓ Successfully converted {self.converted_count} IOCs to {target_format.upper()}")\n                print(f"✓ Saved to {output_file}")\n                if self.failed_count > 0:\n                    print(f"⚠ {self.failed_count} IOCs failed to convert")\n            else:\n                print("✗ Conversion failed")\n            \n            return success\n        except Exception as e:\n            print(f"Conversion error: {e}", file=sys.stderr)\n            return False\n\n\ndef main():\n    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="Convert IOCs between different formats")\n    parser.add_argument("--input", required=True, help="Input IOC file (JSON)")\n    parser.add_argument("--output", required=True, help="Output file path")\n    parser.add_argument("--format", required=True, \n                       choices=["json", "csv", "stix", "openioc"],\n                       help="Target format")\n    parser.add_argument("--pretty", action="store_true", \n                       help="Pretty-print JSON output")\n    \n    args = parser.parse_args()\n    \n    converter = IOCFormatConverter()\n    success = converter.convert(args.input, args.output, args.format)\n    \n    if not success:\n        sys.exit(1)\n\n\nif __name__ == "__main__":\n    main()\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

Let me start with the attribution guide.\n\n\n<function_calls><create-file file_path='V-Sentinel-IOCs/docs/attribution_guide.md'>\n# Threat Attribution Methodology Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nThis document outlines V-Sentinel's methodology for threat actor attribution, confidence levels, and the standards used to assign malicious activity to specific groups.\n\n---\n\n## Attribution Framework\n\n### Confidence Levels\n\nV-Sentinel uses three-tier confidence levels for threat attribution:\n\n#### High Confidence\n- **Definition**: Multiple independent sources corroborate attribution\n- **Requirements**:\n  - Technical evidence (code similarities, infrastructure overlap)\n  - Official government advisories or private intelligence reports\n  - Consistent Tactics, Techniques, and Procedures (TTPs)\n  - Multiple independent security firm reports\n- **Examples**: APT29 (SolarWinds), Lazarus Group (WannaCry)\n\n#### Medium Confidence\n- **Definition**: Technical evidence with some attribution uncertainty\n- **Requirements**:\n  - Code similarities or shared infrastructure\n  - Industry consensus among security researchers\n  - Overlapping TTPs but missing definitive proof\n- **Examples**: Emotet (TA542), LockBit affiliates\n\n#### Low Confidence\n- **Definition**: Single source or circumstantial evidence\n- **Requirements**:\n  - Single security firm report\n  - Limited technical evidence\n  - Industry speculation without definitive proof\n- **Examples**: Emerging threat groups, single incident analysis\n\n---\n\n## Attribution Criteria\n\n### 1. Technical Evidence\n\n#### Code Analysis\n- **Source Code Similarities**: Identical or similar code segments\n- **Compiler Timestamps**: Matching compilation dates\n- **Code Signing Certificates**: Shared or related certificates\n- **Obfuscation Techniques**: Similar encoding methods\n\n#### Infrastructure Overlap\n- **IP Address Ranges**: Related or adjacent IP blocks\n- **Domain Registration**: Similar registrar patterns\n- **Hosting Providers**: Shared hosting infrastructure\n- **DNS Configuration**: Similar DNS setups\n\n#### Malware Family\n- **Family Relationship**: Variants of known malware families\n- **Builder Tools**: Usage of common malware construction kits\n- **Packaging**: Similar packing or obfuscation methods\n\n### 2. Behavioral Patterns\n\n#### Victimology\n- **Target Geography**: Geographic targeting patterns\n- **Industry Sector**: Specific industry focus\n- **Organization Size**: Preference for certain organization sizes\n- **Timing**: Attack timing patterns\n\n#### Operational Security\n- **Language**: Language used in code comments, UI, or communications\n- **Time Zones**: Activity patterns matching specific time zones\n- **Tool Preferences**: Preference for specific tools or frameworks\n- **Error Messages**: Similar error messages or debug strings\n\n### 3. Intelligence Sources\n\n#### Government Advisories\n- CISA (Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency)\n- NSA (National Security Agency)\n- FBI (Federal Bureau of Investigation)\n- International partners (NCSC, ACSC, etc.)\n\n#### Private Intelligence\n- Mandiant\n- CrowdStrike\n- Kaspersky\n- Proofpoint\n- Group-IB\n\n#### Industry Reports\n- Microsoft Threat Intelligence\n- Palo Alto Networks Unit 42\n- Symantec\n- McAfee Advanced Threat Research\n\n---\n\n## Attribution Process\n\n### Phase 1: Data Collection\n1. **IOC Extraction**: Extract all indicators of compromise\n2. **Malware Analysis**: Analyze malware samples\n3. **Network Analysis**: Examine network traffic and infrastructure\n4. **Timeline Reconstruction**: Build attack timeline\n\n### Phase 2: Evidence Correlation\n1. **Cross-Reference**: Compare with known threat actor profiles\n2. **TTP Matching**: Match to MITRE ATT&CK techniques\n3. **Infrastructure Analysis**: Correlate with known infrastructure\n4. **Code Comparison**: Compare with known malware samples\n\n### Phase 3: Confidence Assessment\n1. **Evidence Scoring**: Score each piece of evidence\n2. **Source Evaluation**: Evaluate source reliability\n3. **Independence Check**: Verify source independence\n4. **Consistency Check**: Ensure consistency across sources\n\n### Phase 4: Attribution Assignment\n1. **Threat Actor Identification**: Identify most likely threat actor\n2. **Confidence Assignment**: Assign appropriate confidence level\n3. **Documentation**: Document all evidence and reasoning\n4. **Peer Review**: Conduct internal peer review\n\n---\n\n## Common Attribution Pitfalls\n\n### 1. Single Source Attribution\n**Problem**: Relying on a single source without corroboration\n**Solution**: Require multiple independent sources for high confidence\n\n### 2. Infrastructure Reuse\n**Problem**: Attributing based solely on shared infrastructure\n**Solution**: Infrastructure reuse is common; require additional evidence\n\n### 3. Malware-as-a-Service\n**Problem**: Attributing to operator when malware is rented\n**Solution**: Differentiate between malware developers and operators\n\n### 4. False Flags\n**Problem**: Threat actors planting false attribution clues\n**Solution**: Be skeptical of obvious attribution markers\n\n### 5. Political Bias\n**Problem**: Politically motivated attributions\n**Solution**: Maintain objectivity and follow evidence\n\n---\n\n## Case Studies\n\n### Case 1: APT29 - SolarWinds Supply Chain Attack\n\n**Evidence Collected**:\n- Code similarities to previous APT29 operations\n- Infrastructure overlap with known APT29 servers\n- Targeting consistent with Russian state interests\n- Multiple government attributions (NSA, CISA, UK NCSC)\n\n**Confidence Level**: High\n\n**Attribution Process**:\n1. Identified Sunburst backdoor in SolarWinds Orion\n2. Analyzed C2 infrastructure (avsvmcloud.com)\n3. Correlated with previous APT29 TTPs\n4. Reviewed multiple independent reports\n5. Confirmed with government advisories\n\n### Case 2: Lazarus Group - WannaCry Ransomware\n\n**Evidence Collected**:\n- Code similarities to Lazarus Group malware\n- Infrastructure overlap with known Lazarus servers\n- Timing consistent with North Korean operations\n- Multiple private intelligence firm reports\n\n**Confidence Level**: High\n\n**Attribution Process**:\n1. Analyzed WannaCry ransomware samples\n2. Identified code segments matching Lazarus tools\n3. Correlated with North Korean time zone activity\n4. Reviewed intelligence from multiple firms\n5. Confirmed with government advisories\n\n---\n\n## Attribution Ethics\n\n### Responsible Attribution\n\n1. **Evidence-Based**: Attribution must be based on technical evidence\n2. **Transparency**: Clearly state confidence levels and evidence\n3. **Independence**: Use multiple independent sources\n4. **Avoid Speculation**: Don't speculate without evidence\n5. **Update**: Update attributions as new evidence emerges\n\n### When NOT to Attribute\n\n1. **Single Source**: Without corroboration from other sources\n2. **Circumstantial Evidence**: Without technical evidence\n3. **Politically Motivated**: When attribution serves political agendas\n4. **Commercially Motivated**: When attribution serves commercial interests\n5. **Insufficient Evidence**: When evidence is inconclusive\n\n---\n\n## Attribution Standards\n\n### MITRE ATT&CK Framework\n\nV-Sentinel maps all attributed threats to MITRE ATT&CK techniques:\n- **Tactics**: High-level goals\n- **Techniques**: Methods to achieve tactics\n- **Procedures**: Specific implementations\n\n### STIX 2.1 Format\n\nAll attributed threats are documented in STIX 2.1 format:\n- **Identity Objects**: Threat actor identities\n- **Intrusion Set Objects**: Groupings of related attacks\n- **Indicator Objects**: Technical indicators\n- **Relationship Objects**: Connections between objects\n\n### Industry Standards\n\nV-Sentinel follows industry attribution standards:\n- **FIRST**: Forum of Incident Response and Security Teams\n- **ISAC**: Information Sharing and Analysis Centers\n- **ENISA**: European Union Agency for Cybersecurity\n- **ISO/IEC 27001**: Information security management\n\n---\n\n## Attribution Updates\n\n### Review Process\n\nAttributions are reviewed quarterly or when new evidence emerges:\n1. **Evidence Review**: Review new evidence\n2. **Confidence Reassessment**: Reassess confidence levels\n3. **Attribution Updates**: Update or modify attributions\n4. **Documentation**: Document changes and reasoning\n\n### Version Control\n\nAll attributions are version controlled:\n- **Major Updates**: Significant new evidence requiring reattribution\n- **Minor Updates**: Additional evidence supporting existing attribution\n- **Corrections**: Corrections to previous attributions\n\n---\n\n## Contact\n\nFor questions about threat attribution:\n- **Security Research Team**: security-research@vantis.ai\n- **Attribution Questions**: attribution@vantis.ai\n- **Report Errors**: Use GitHub Issues\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n- [MITRE ATT&CK](https://attack.mitre.org/)\n- [CISA Advisory Catalog](https://www.cisa.gov/news-events/cybersecurity-advisories)\n- [Mandiant Threat IOC Data Structure\nEach IOC record includes:\n- **Identification**: Unique ID, type, value\n- **Temporal Data**: First seen, last seen timestamps\n- **Threat Intelligence**: Threat actor, campaign, malware family\n- **Confidence**: Low, medium, high confidence levels\n- **Metadata**: Description, tags, references\n- **Technical Details**: DNS info, file info, certificates\n\n### 3.  "aliases": ["Cozy Bear", "The Dukes", "Yttrium"],\n  "country": "Russia",\n  "motivation": "Espionage",\n  "attribution_confidence": "high",\n  "mitre_attack": "G0016",\n  "campaigns": ["SolarWinds Supply Chain Attack", "2016 US Election Interference"],\n  "indicators": [\n    {\n      "id": "apt29-001",\n      "type": "ip",\n      "value": "185.141.63.22",\n      "confidence": "high",\n      "description": "Command and control server",\n      "campaign": "SolarWinds Supply Chain Attack",\n      "malware_family": "Sunburst",\n      "tags": ["c2", "solarwinds", "apt"]\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n### Automation Capabilities\n\n#### IOC Generation\n- Generate IP, domain, URL, hash, and email IOCs\n- Support for multiple threat actors and campaigns\n- Configurable IOC counts and confidence levels\n- Metadata enrichment\n\n#### IOC Validation\n- JSON schema validation\n- IOC type validation (IP, domain, URL, hash, email, certificate)\n- Date consistency checking\n- Duplicate detection\n- Strict mode for production use\n\n#### Format Conversion\n- JSON → CSV\n- JSON → STIX 2.1\n- JSON → OpenIOC XML\n- Pretty-printed JSON output\n\n### Detection Rules\n\n#### YARA Rules\n- SolarWinds Sunburst backdoor detection\n- Teardrop lateral movement detection\n- AppleJeus trojan detection\n- Manuscrypt stealer detection\n- WannaCry ransomware detection\n- Generic APT detection patterns\n\n#### Snort Rules\n- C2 traffic detection\n- DNS tunneling detection\n- Lateral movement detection\n- Data exfiltration detection\n- Known malicious IP/domain blocking\n\n---\n\n## 📚 Documentation Highlights\n\n### Attribution Methodology\n- **Three-tier confidence levels**: High, Medium, Low\n- **Evidence-based attribution**: Code analysis, infrastructure overlap, behavioral patterns\n- **Attribution process**: 4-phase systematic approach\n- **Ethical guidelines**: Responsible attribution standards\n- **Case studies**: APT29 SolarWinds, Lazarus WannaCry\n\n### Contribution Guidelines\n- **IOC format requirements**: Detailed JSON schema\n- **Detection rule standards**: YARA, Snort, Sigma formats\n- **Validation procedures**: Automated testing requirements\n- \'ip\']\n\n# Check against network traffic\ndef is_malicious(ip):\n    return ip in malicious_ips\n```\n\n### SIEM Integration (Splunk)\n```splunk\nindex=network \n| lookup iocs.json indicator AS dest_ip OUTPUT threat_actor, campaign, severity\n| where isnotnull(threat_actor)\n| table _time, dest_ip, threat_actor, campaign, severity\n```\n\n### Firewall Integration (Palo Alto)\n```bash\n# Invalid API key\n    - Expired API key\n    - Insufficient permissions\n    """\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        message: str = "Authentication failed",\n        details: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None,\n    ) -> None:\n        super().__init__(message, status_code=401, details=details)\n\n\nclass RateLimitError(VSentinelError):\n    """\n    Raised when rate limit is exceeded.\n    \n    Args:\n        retry_after: Seconds to wait before retrying\n        message: Error message\n    """\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        retry_after: int = 60,\n        message: str = "Rate limit exceeded",\n    ) -> None:\n        super().__init__(message, status_code=429)\n        self.retry_after = retry_after\n    \n    def __str__(self) -> str:\n        return f"Rate limit exceeded. Retry after {self.retry_after} seconds."\n\n\nclass ResourceNotFoundError(VSentinelError):\n    """\n    Raised when a requested resource is not found.\n    \n    Args:\n        resource: Type of resource that was not found\n        resource_id: ID of the resource (if applicable)\n        message: Error message\n    """\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        resource: str = "Resource",\n        resource_id: Optional[str] = None,\n        message: Optional[str] = None,\n    ) -> None:\n        if message is None:\n            if resource_id:\n                message = f"{resource} with ID \'{resource_id}\' not found"\n            else:\n                message = f"{resource} not found"\n        \n        super().__init__(message, status_code=404)\n        self.resource = resource\n        self.resource_id = resource_id\n\n\nclass ValidationError(VSentinelError):\n    """\n    Raised when request validation fails.\n    \n    Args:\n        message: Error message\n        field: Field that failed validation\n        details: Validation error details\n    """\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        message: str = "Validation error",\n        field: Optional[str] = None,\n        details: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None,\n    ) -> None:\n        super().__init__(message, status_code=400, details=details)\n        self.field = field\n\n\nclass ConnectionError(VSentinelError):\n    """\n    Raised when connection to V-Sentinel API fails.\n    \n    This typically means:\n    - Network connectivity issues\n    - API server is down\n    - DNS resolution failure\n    """\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        message: str = "Failed to connect to V-Sentinel API",\n        details: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None,\n    ) -> None:\n        super().__init__(message, details=details)\n\n\nclass TimeoutError(VSentinelError):\n    """\n    Raised when a request times out.\n    \n    Args:\n        timeout: Timeout duration in seconds\n    """\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        timeout: int = 30,\n        message: Optional[str] = None,\n    ) -> None:\n        if message is None:\n            message = f"Request timed out after {timeout} seconds"\n        super().__init__(message)\n        self.timeout = timeout\n\n\nclass ConfigurationError(VSentinelError):\n    """\n    Raised when SDK configuration is invalid.\n    \n    This typically means:\n    - Missing required configuration\n    - Invalid configuration values\n    - Environment variables not set\n    """\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        message: str = "Invalid configuration",\n        details: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None,\n    ) -> None:\n        super().__init__(message, details=details)\n\n\nclass MCPError(VSentinelError):\n    """\n    Raised when MCP (Model Context Protocol) operation fails.\n    \n    Args:\n        tool: Name of the MCP tool that failed\n        operation: Operation that failed\n    """\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        tool: str,\n        operation: str,\n        message: Optional[str] = None,\n        details: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None,\n    ) -> None:\n        if message is None:\n            message = f"MCP operation \'{operation}\' failed for tool \'{tool}\'"\n        super().__init__(message, details=details)\n        self.tool = tool\n        self.operation = operation\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}
